< text>
I have rented a small house from Cal Oaks Property Mgmt for 13 years and I have always paid my rent on time, and they have been very responsive with property maintenance issues when I needed their help.     I had an Oven/range they replaced about 5 years ago, a microwave/vent fan they recently replaced last month (13 years old), a hot water heater they replaced two years ago (11 years old),  1 minor plumbing problem they had fixed, and a roof leak about 4 years ago that they had repaired after a series of hard rains, all within a few days.     In all instances, Cal Oaks staff & their contractors responded quickly.     Even when my water heater went out on a late Fri night they had it fixed by 11 AM on Saturday.    Appliance repairs/replacements  were done by Winkler Appliance Repair and once they got the authorization from Cal Oaks they fixed or replaced the appliance issues within a few days.         In a tight and expensive rental market, they run a business, but I've been happy with their responsiveness and having a good place to live.< /text>

< Review>
Owned a bike of one sort or another for 35 years now.  In that course I've dealt with over a dozen shops.  I can easily sort them into two categories: 1) all the others and 2) Berkeley Yamaha Honda.  My first experience was two years ago when  new model I had purchased at another dealership required a filter for the break in service that hadn't hit dealer shelves yet.  Well after calling every dealer in Bay Area, Karl was the one and only guy to call me the next week when he got one in.  So after that treatment (on such a low markup service mind you) I've gone there consistently.  All services - great price, outstanding service each and every time.  On my way home I stopped in with slow leak in rear tire - caught them at a busy time - storeroom full of other customers.  30 minutes later I'm a scant few dollars lighter in the wallet and back on the road on a tire that needed no more attention until replacement time.  How good are they? - I am often tripped up when considering a new bike by any other manufacturer than Honda or Yamaha, because I appreciate their business so much.  They are the best!<//Review>

<user_id>116198101286360774030< /user_id><Rating>5<//Rating><GmapID>0x80857ed1611aa087:0x533f15342aa6bae8</GmapID><text>Honest.

This is the best place to buy a bike from. I can't speak to the service department, but the sales staff were honest and helpful. They went out of their way to help me deal with a title issue on my used bike and went above and beyond what I expected from a dealer. They inquired several times about my issue at the DMV main office in Sacramento and kept updating me about the status. Ultimately they saved me from a few trips to the DMV as well as a pretty big fine (long story - not my fault, not their fault). They even offered to pay my registration as a token of good faith for the hassle (even though it was not their fault). This is not the kind of experience I expected to have with a dealership. Makes me want to buy my next bike from them, even though I don't live in the Bay anymore.

Bottom line: This is a great shop with knowledgeable and honest owner / employees. I would gladly buy my next bike from them.<//text>< username>

<date>1574119677069</date><user_name>Jared Cohee</user_name>< review>
M√âXICO (NAYARIT) üá≤üáΩ
Excerpt from Eat the World Los Angeles:
The Mexican state of Nayarit is no stranger to Los Angeles, with many families claiming roots there and the coastal cuisine living large in the lives of many Angelenos. This usually consists of plates of freshly prepared mariscos, unique ceviches, and the awe-inspiring pescado zarandeado, but a tiny little Pacoima joint has been hawking the tamales of Nayarit for around ten years.

"Estilo Nayarit" is actually quite easy to miss on the sign, especially while flying by on wide Glenoaks Blvd. With the holidays approaching, there will be many feelings about tamales to go around, but for those without stacks of them made at home, Rosy's is a unique find to enjoy the recipes that trace their origin to the owner's hometown of Zacualpan.

Even coming in from the blazing summer sun, there is an enjoyment to eating a tamal with a cup of hot champurrado, always available here at Rosy's. What can be less easy to find are the chicken tamales, the stars of the show, which are frequently sold out. Fresh batches are prepared throughout the morning (Rosy's closes at 13:00) though, so if your timing is not perfect on the first visit, just try again another day. Start with the tamal de pollo en salsa verde, which they have covered with a handwritten "HOT" notice on their board. The sauce is green because of an ample use of jalape√±os, and is always made fresh.< /review>

< Review>
On 6/17/2016 at 1pm, What an experience visiting this Burger King, unbelievable it needs 25cents to use the bathroom, after I finished ordering, I requested one of the girl at the counter for the bathroom key, she gave me 5 cents instead of 25 cents, I told her that was not enough and she ignored me, I was standing there for about 30 minutes waiting for my order and a quarter for the bathroom,  She was busy at the register, I kept reminding her about the bathroom issue, she did not seem to care, at the same time, my order was not ready either!  Actually my order was at that kitchen window, but no one care to give it to me until I asked, it took about half an hour for me to get my food and finally I got the quarter for use of the bathroom not until I was upset.
It is not acceptable for a fast food restaurant to keep customer waiting their food for 30 minutes in a moderate customer day, my order was just a hotdog meal and a single hotdog basic.
The service was so terrible due to under manpower, Any fast food restaurant try to make bathroom money Will not last too long, and I will not recommend this Burger King to anyone at all.< /Review>

< Text>
I have been a Forever21 customer since I was in middle school (now I am 19.) I have always been content with my products, and have rarely ever returned an item (if I do, I exchange it for something that fits.)
For the past year, I have noticed a huge drop in customer service provider by the employees at the Forever21 location in Stockton. I could probably spend an hour in the store without being greeted, helped, or even looked at by the teenage/young adult employees.
Now, I am myself a cashier and returns employee for Marshalls, and every customer I am NEAR, I am supposed to greet and ask if I could be of help. When I am to check out customers, I am supposed to acknowledge my customers. Heres where Forever21 is different from Marshalls: Don't expect any customer service. Any.
On the last two occasions I have visited Forever21, i have had horrible experiences with the careless staff.
My first horrible experience, I was shopping with my boyfriend (it was my birthday, so he took me shopping for my presents.) i had Eleven items to try on, and they let me enter the dressing room with Nine items. The other two were "hung by the associate on my dressingroom door." No, they weren't. If they were - someone took them off my door and misplaced them. I asked an associate why my items were misplaced and all she said was "i dont know, i hung them on your door." I asked another associate if she saw the items, but she was rude and would only repeat "they were on the door." No help to locate my items, or even apologize for the issue. I left the store angry at their horrible and zero attempts at customer service.
I visited the same store with my mother in the hopes of finding a swimsuit. I tried it on in the fittingrooms, but I wasn't too sure on the swimsuit. When I walked up to the registers, BEFORE PURCHASING MY ITEM, I asked what the store policy was on Returning Swimsuits. My cashier, Caitlin, told me I had thirty days to return the items with the tags still attached and unworn. Then, she double-checked with a so-called manager, and she told me the same thing Caitlin did. So, I went on with purchasing the swimsuit.
A week later, on July 8th, I went to the store to return the swimsuit. Cashier Wendy would not accept my return for "sanitary reasons", even though I explained to her what employees had told me. She said in that case, she could only return the swim top as a favor of customer service. Ha! Wendy was so rude to begin with, my boyfriend asked for the Manager. Wendy CLAIMED she was the MANAGER, and told us that there was nothing she could do for the mistakes of her employees (whom clearly needed to be taught the store policies). We left the store and immediately called it from the parkinglot. Wendy picked up, and we asked for a manager. She never oncr revealed she was the manager, and instead put us on hold for the REAL STORE MANAGER. But Wendy put us on hold for fove minutes and nobody ever answered. We called back, and they blamed their rude customer service on how busy the store was (which it wasnt - we were just in there.) Finally reaching the manager, she complately apologized for Wendys behavior and told me I could come back and return my swim suit bottoms for a store credit, since they do accept unwanted returns "sometimes." i went in there to return my item and the manager asked for my information/I.D. like I was turning in stolen items (I had the receipt which was the only thing I needed to make a return at Forever21.) After giving them my information (which I feel was completely unnecessary) they issued my store credit.
Never setting foot in the Stockton Forever21 ever again, and I will strongly consider ever shopping at the retailer again.< /Text>

<UserId.>114100504603957937532<//UserId.><user_name>Claire de Lune< /user_name><time>1435562037361<//time><Rate>1< /Rate>< review>
On April 3, 2015 I sent a message to Forever 21's Facebook page regarging the situation at the store located at the Weberstown Mall in Stockton, CA. Here is an excerpt of what I wrote:

"I am utterly disappointed and disgusted with the appearance of one of your stores in Stockton, CA. I went there on Monday, March 30, 2015 and found the store disgustingly dirty and chaotic. Every single time I went there one would think that the customers are just plain disrespectful and ghetto to wreck havoc into a store and pity the workers who would have to clean and re-arrange them every hour, every day.

But as I came back to the same store on Thursday, April 2, 2015, it was still the same mess. The thing that led me to think that it is the employees and not the customers who are disgusting. There are dust bunnies all over the store.. Yes, dust bunnies. Those little furry clumps of dust do not grow overnight. Not only that. Pieces of tissue paper can be found all over the floor, broken hangers, jewelry and clothing and electrical plugs where people can trip on. A shelf for $3.90 short sleeved tees is overrun by an enormous pile of knitted leggings and not a shirt could be found in that mess.

I am attaching pictures that I took to prove what I am talking about. Also, check the facebook page of Forever21 Stockon and read the  the reviews. Another customer has posted about the mess last year and it seems like it has been and will be an on going problem if nothing is to be done."

---End of excerpt---

Then on June 28, 2015 I visited again the store. It is still as filthy as it looked last time. Nothing changed except for the worst.

Do you guys even know how filthy a dust bunny is? They are small clumps of dust that form under furniture and in corners that are not cleaned regularly. They are made of hair, lint, dead skin, spider webs, dust, and sometimes light rubbish and debris, and are held together by static electricity and felt-like entanglement

From what I observed the employees never mopped or swept the floor in years! That is disgusting. And with all the clothes on the floor that they put back on the racks full of dust just send shivers to my spine.

The Facebook page of Forever 21 responded by saying: "We've issued these complaints to our upper management team and we certainly look forward to finding resolve. We'll be contacting you soon regarding this matter. Thanks so much again!"

They never contacted me nor resolved the problem. I don't even know if this was reported to the upper management. And I don't think it will take 2 months to resolve this problem.

Have I ever told an employee about my concerns? NO. I don't think it is rocket science to figure out how disgusting a store is.

From,
Somebody who used to love the brand but now feels disgusted by it.</review>

< text>
On a road trip from San Diego going up the coast, I made an appointment about a week prior for a wheel/tire swap on my GT4.
Making the appointment was easy online. Had good followup through text which I appreciated.

I was about 30 min early, and they didn't seem to mind. I was put with Weis Popal as my advisor. Explained to him the scenario- I'm from out of town, in a slight hurry, another customer would be dropping off a set of wheels that I wanted to put on the car so I just needed the tires and TPMS from my current wheels swapped over. Easy enough.

Not only did it they have a quick turnaround time, but Weis went above and beyond to keep me in the loop during the process.

But where he far exceeded my expectations from ANY dealer was his help and generosity with providing me a space and direct help with facilitating the packing and shipping of my other set of wheels. He even casually involved some behind the scenes people to make sure I was set up and taken care of.

I no longer do- but as I had previously worked for over a decade in the car world, specifically high end dealerships, I know that this sort of assistance and customer care is not only rare- but virtually non existent. Almost always falling over to the "Not any of my business" type of mentality. He made it his business. Not only did this dramatically decrease the time I had to spend on this project, but made it exponentially more convenient for me on my trip.

This is the level of customer service you would expect from a brand like Porsche, and I'm sure they are happy to have someone like Mr. Popal be the face that assists their clients. Thank you again.</text>

< Review>
After searching U.S. for Audi S5, low mileage & $30K budget, finally found at Sonnen Porsche. Michael Gray (sales) checked with manager and said they accept our offer (even beat the best deal on CarGurus website). We drove same day and bought wife's dream car, clean report, 1 owner, well-maintained. Michael was professional and humorous, absolutely no pressure to buy.
Emil (finance) was courteous and professional. Some bank pre-approval confusion, but found similar APR % and went with another bank. Finally, bought extended warranty, good rating on BBB website. But after researching more quotes, nearly canceled warranty purchased. Emil was patient and worked to extend warranty terms for similar price.

< Review>
I cannot really praise Brett Payne @ Sonnen/Marin Porsche too highly.

Too often when you interact with a Sales Guy, even a Porsche Sales guy, you look back on the experience wondering in what creative way they screwed you?

This is *not* the case with Brett, I have bought one 911 from him, and thanks to his honesty and diligence, I have just ordered another.

What distinguished Brett from other salesman? Firstly he loves the cars,
when Brett specifies car car for the show floor, you can expect that he
has not simply loaded it with expensive options, but he has ordered a
car that he, or another 911 aficionado would order.

Secondly, he's honest and professional; when you interact with him, you know that what he's telling you is fact, not fiction, spin, false news, or
simply what you want to hear in order to get the sale!

I honestly did not think when I put my deposit on my new 911, that being #13 on the list I would get an allocation, but Brett assured me, that based
on past experiences, I would get one, and guess what, I did - he was right!

Brett is not your average car sales guy, he's not even your average Porsche brand ambassador, he's exemplary, he will continue to get my business and my highest recommendation possible...

Brett (and Gary Wright in the service dept) are the reason that Sonnen get my highest recommendation, and continued business.

I recently bought an $80,000 CPO Cayman GTS from Marin and have had a horrid experience with some rattles from day one. Some plastic trim panels in the trunk are clearly loose and move about and I have shared videos of the rattle with the service department. In spite of this, after three months and three appointments they have not been able to fix the problem.

Let me be clear - Andrew is awesome, he helped me a ton even after I bought the car from him. Gary, Adam and the technicians are amazing - they go out of their way to help you, as much as possible.

However the new service director, Kevin is clueless, arrogant and unprofessional. He comes from VW and treats customers at that level. The entire service department seems under tremendous pressure and it takes two to three weeks to just get an appointment. It takes less time to get an appointment with my doctor at Stanford!

Because of this mis-management, when you finally bring your car in they are slow and do a half-hearted job. I recently brought my car in a third time to fix the same rattle and Kevin kept my car for eight days. He promised he‚Äôd have the foreman look at it but when I finally collected the car absolutely nothing had been fixed. To add insult to injury he told me some BS stories but the GPS tracker on my car clearly shows my car stayed parked and they did no test drives to isolate or fix the core issue. By the way, I always had to call and check-in since I recd. no courtesy updates from his side. Like I said, clueless, arrogant and unprofessional. Instead of enjoying my car I will now have to follow up with Porsche North America about all of this.

Other things I didn‚Äôt appreciate. After you buy a car or after a service they will pressurize you to give them great reviews. I can also vouch, like some other reviews, that their receptionists and some others can be uptight and rude. A lot of people who work here don‚Äôt seem too happy or professional in general and it maps to a negative experience.

My perception of Porsche has changed thanks to Porsche Marin. Almost every Porsche dealership in the Bay Area has better reviews. Take your hard earned money elsewhere.</Review>
